Use a[0], a[1], ... to access elements in an array, a.length is the length (note that s.length() is for Strings). Allocate a new array like this: int[] a = new int[10];  // length 10 array <br/>See the <a href="/doc/array.html">Java Arrays and Loops Help</a> document for help.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p185685">firstLast6</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p118976">sameFirstLast</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p167011">makePi</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>

Recursion strategy: first test for one or two base cases that are so  simple, the answer can be returned immediately.  Otherwise, make a recursive a call for a smaller case  (that is, a case which is a step towards the base case).  Assume that the recursive call works correctly, and fix  up what it returns to make the answer.<br/></p><table><tr><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p154669">factorial</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p183649">bunnyEars</a> <font color="gray">H</font> </td><td width="200"> <img src="/c1.jpg"/><a href="/prob/p120015">fibonacci</a></td></tr>
